Priority 1 Accessibility


P1 - Manual check

There are some checkpoints that an automatic program like Bobby cannot examine. These 5 item(s) are presented below. You will need to be able to respond affirmatively to these items as well to obtain Bobby Approved status.
  1. Provide alternative content for each SCRIPT that conveys important information or function. (1 instance)

Congratulations! This web page contains no accessibility errors that Bobby can detect. There are, however, some checkpoints that an automatic program like Bobby cannot examine. These item(s) are presented above. You must be able to respond to these questions affirmatively in order to obtain Bobby Approval.

Priority 2 Accessibility

Bobby Approved status is assigned on the basis of Priority 1 items in the Web Content Guidelines. For a higher level of accessibility you may also want to examine Priority 2 and Priority 3 items. No Priority 2 items that Bobby is able to detect have been found, but you should examine the list of items that require a manual examination below. To achieve conformance with Priority 2 guidelines you need to be able to answer affirmatively to these items.

P2 - Manual check

In addition to the items that Bobby can examine there are 5 Priority 2 issue(s) presented below for which Bobby cannot make a determination. To achieve conformance with Priority 2 guidelines you need to be able to answer affirmatively to these items.

    Line 451: <div class="digi-coll-body"><p>Representative Poetry Online includes 4,079 English poems by 618 poets from Caedmon, in the Old English period, to the work of living poets today. It is based on Representative Poetry, established by Professor W. J. Alexander of University College, University of Toronto, in 1912 and used in the English Department at the University until the late 1960s. Its electronic founder and editor since 1994 is <a href="http://rpo.library.utoronto.ca/display_rpo/edition/lancashire.html" target="_blank">Ian Lancashire</a>, who is a member of the Department of English, University of Toronto.</p>

  5. Mark up quotations with the Q and BLOCKQUOTE elements.



Priority 3 Accessibility

Bobby Approved status is assigned on the basis of Priority 1 items in the Web Content Guidelines. For a higher level of accessibility you may also want to examine Priority 2 and Priority 3 items. No Priority 3 items that Bobby is able to detect have been found, but you should examine the list of items that require a manual examination below. To achieve conformance with Priority 3 guidelines you need to be able to answer affirmatively to these items.

P3 - Manual check

In addition to the items that Bobby can examine there are 3 Priority 3 issue(s) presented below for which Bobby cannot make a determination. To achieve conformance with Priority 3 guidelines you need to be able to answer affirmatively to these items.
  1. Use the ABBR and ACRONYM elements to denote and expand abbreviations and acronyms.

  2. Identify the language of the text, and any changes in the language.

  3. Consider adding keyboard shortcuts to frequently used links. (296 instances)

    Line 296: <div class="digi-coll-image"><a href="http://link.library.utoronto.ca/cpp/"><img typeof="foaf:Image" src="sites/default/files/xcpp.jpg.pagespeed.ic.nJUzNZIzmF.jpg" alt="Canadian Printer and Publisher" title="Canadian Printer and Publisher" width="70" height="70"/></a></div>
    Line 297: <div class="digi-coll-body"><p>Canadian Printer and Publisher, which began in 1892 and is still being published today by Rogers Media under the title <a href="http://www.bizlink.com/canadianprinter.htm">Canadian Printer Magazine</a>, is the national organ of the printing industry in Canada. It documents the growth and evolution of the trade, during a period of continuous technological and commercial innovation, beginning in the period when machine composition was taking over from hand composition in the 1890s.</p>

    Line 450: <div class="digi-coll-image"><a href="http://rpo.library.utoronto.ca/"><img typeof="foaf:Image" src="sites/default/files/xblake_0.gif.pagespeed.ic.hdpsifuxU4.png" alt="Representative Poetry Online" title="Representative Poetry Online" width="55" height="70"/></a></div>
    Line 451: <div class="digi-coll-body"><p>Representative Poetry Online includes 4,079 English poems by 618 poets from Caedmon, in the Old English period, to the work of living poets today. It is based on Representative Poetry, established by Professor W. J. Alexander of University College, University of Toronto, in 1912 and used in the English Department at the University until the late 1960s. Its electronic founder and editor since 1994 is <a href="http://rpo.library.utoronto.ca/display_rpo/edition/lancashire.html" target="_blank">Ian Lancashire</a>, who is a member of the Department of English, University of Toronto.</p>
